## Notes & Gotchas

- **A stuck-background-wait subagent can leave an orphaned process tree running that actively competes for CPU with a sibling dimension's own validate run — check for and kill these during worktree inspection, not just resume the stuck agent (run 42):** After resuming D4 (stuck waiting on its own backgrounded `pnpm run validate`) with a "stop waiting, report now" message, its original shell process and validate chain kept running unsupervised in the background (the resume ends the agent's _turn_, not its spawned child processes). That leftover chain progressed on to `pnpm test` and was still consuming significant CPU minutes later, at the same time D5's own genuine (and much slower than usual) `eslint` run was competing for cores in a sibling worktree. **Takeaway: whenever you inspect a worktree during stuck-agent recovery, also `ps aux` for that worktree's path and check whether the agent's original background command is still alive after you've told it to stop waiting — if the diff is already resolved (empty, or already captured), kill the leftover process tree (`kill -9`) rather than leaving it to silently consume shared CPU for the rest of the run.**
- **When a genuinely long dimension diff (e.g., a JSX reindent from removing a wrapper fragment) makes eslint/vitest run unusually slowly, don't assume something is broken — but DO independently take over verification once a subagent's own background check is taking a long time, rather than waiting indefinitely on it (run 42):** D5's `eslint` run took 5+ minutes (mostly due to the D4 CPU contention above), well past what a subagent typically waits before ending its turn. Rather than resuming D5's own agent repeatedly, the orchestrator used a `Monitor` until-loop keyed on the specific eslint PID to wait for it to exit, then ran the rest of `validate` + `build` itself directly in the worktree — this is a valid and often faster alternative to a resume-loop when the orchestrator already has full worktree/bash access and the subagent's job (finding + committing the fix) is done; the orchestrator doesn't need the subagent's own turn to run verification commands it's equally capable of running itself.
- **A dispatch prompt that explicitly asks a subagent to "investigate deeply and bias toward formalizing as an Intentional Exception over guessing at a fix" is an effective way to clear a long-stalled NEEDS REVIEW backlog cluster without forcing a risky conversion (run 42):** D3's "third tier" `font-bold`-not-`font-black` cluster had sat unresolved across 7 files for 20+ runs. Framing the dispatch as an investigation task (not a "pick one and fix it" task) let the subagent discover the cluster was actually 4 independently-evidenced deliberate tiers (60+, 25+, 4, and 7 confirmed instances via a repo-wide re-grep by class string, not the stale line numbers originally logged) plus one genuine outlier — resolving 6 of 7 backlog rows via new exceptions (D3-E24–E27) with zero code shipped and zero risk of flattening real design intent. The orchestrator independently spot-checked each of the four proposed tiers via its own grep before accepting them into the canon — worth continuing to do even when a subagent's evidence looks thorough, since accepting a wrong "it's deliberate" claim into the canon is exactly as bad as wrongly flattening real drift. **Takeaway: for backlog items that have resisted resolution over many runs, consider a dedicated "investigate and classify, don't guess-fix" dispatch rather than repeatedly re-offering them as one-of-several candidate targets — the investigation itself can be the night's deliverable.**
- **`components/layout/Dock.tsx:1586`'s D2 NEEDS REVIEW item has now sat unresolved since run 30 (12+ consecutive runs) with an explicit "do not fix in isolation, human decision needed" flag — worth escalating to the human operator directly rather than just re-logging it silently forever (run 42):** Re-confirmed present and correctly untouched again this run. Since this item genuinely cannot be resolved by any future nightly dispatch (the fix requires either accepting it as permanent chrome or scoping a coordinated multi-instance re-theme, both human calls), continuing to silently re-verify it every ~5 runs without escalating serves no purpose. Flagged in this run's summary notification to the user; future runs should keep doing the same until a human decision lands, rather than treating "still needs a human decision" as a satisfying terminal state on its own.

- **When a subagent hits the stuck-background-wait failure mode, resuming it via a fresh `Agent` call with the worktree path/branch/git-state restated in the prompt works as a substitute for the documented `SendMessage`-to-the-original-agent resume — but `SendMessage` (addressing the agent by its name/id) is the correct tool and should be preferred going forward (run 41):** D1's subagent ended its turn waiting on a `nohup ... & disown`-backgrounded validate run it had no way to be notified about. The orchestrator inspected the worktree directly first (clean `git status`/`git diff`, a `git reset` in the reflog implying an attempted-then-reverted change, and one genuinely still-running `tsc --noEmit` process), then dispatched a brand-new `general-purpose` agent with the full situation restated (worktree path, branch, what was found, an explicit "do not `nohup`/`&`/`disown`, do not end your turn waiting" instruction) rather than using `SendMessage` to resume the original agent's own transcript/context. This worked cleanly (one round, correct final report, stray process killed) because the worktree's git state is the actual source of truth regardless of which agent process is looking at it — but it discards the original agent's internal reasoning/context for no benefit. **Takeaway: prefer `SendMessage` addressed to the stuck agent (by name, or by its `agentId` if unnamed) to resume it in-context; only fall back to a fresh `Agent` dispatch with restated context if `SendMessage` is unavailable or the original agent/worktree is confirmed gone (per the run-28 note below).**
- **D1's MiniApp `AssignmentsModal.tsx`/`SubmissionsModal.tsx` VISUAL-RISK item now has two independently-reached blocking rationales, not just one — worth citing both in future dispatch prompts (run 41):** The original run-34 framing was purely technical (`absolute inset-0` overlays never establish `container-type: size`, so cqmin sizing wouldn't resolve). Run 41's subagent independently attempted the fix anyway (mirroring the ActivityWall run-35 technique of scoping a `container-type: size` boundary just to the empty-state branch) and reached a second, complementary objection: these are full-page modal overlays outside the `WidgetRegistry` `skipScaling` container-query model entirely, not widget front-faces — imposing a widget-scaling CSS concern onto a non-widget modal surface for a cosmetic empty-state consistency win risks coupling/changing the modal's own layout and stacking-context behavior, a real scope-creep risk disproportionate to the payoff. It reverted cleanly via `git reset` before committing anything. **Takeaway: this item is more solidly blocked than a single technical objection suggested — a future run shouldn't need to re-attempt the ActivityWall-style fix here without a human first deciding the win is worth the modal-layout risk.**
- **A backlog item surfaced by an automated PR reviewer, out of scope for the PR it commented on (run 41):** `claude[bot]`'s review of PR #2263 (D3's SyntaxFramer "Alignment" `SettingsLabel` retrofit) approved the change but flagged a pre-existing, unrelated gap: the two icon-only alignment buttons (`AlignLeft`/`AlignCenter`) in the same component have no `aria-label`. Correctly not fixed in that PR (out of scope — D3's canon is about the label primitive, not icon-button accessibility) and not something this routine's dimensions currently cover. **New backlog item, not yet assigned to a dimension:** a repo-wide sweep for icon-only `<button>`s missing `aria-label`/`aria-labelledby` could be a legitimate future 6th consistency dimension (or folded into an existing one) — flagged here for a human to scope, not acted on.

- **The `Read` tool silently truncates very long single lines (this doc's table rows routinely exceed 2000 chars) without any visible marker — copy-pasting its displayed output into an `Edit` `old_string` can produce a byte-for-byte-looking but actually-truncated string that never matches (run 40):** Two `Edit` calls against this doc's Run Log table header/rows failed with "String to replace not found," even after re-reading the exact line and copying it verbatim from the tool's own output. Root cause: `sed -n '<n>p' docs/routines/unifier.md | wc -c` showed the true line was ~2048 bytes, but `Read`'s rendered output for the same line was shorter and silently missing the trailing `| --- | --- |` cell — no ellipsis, no length warning, nothing to signal the truncation. **Takeaway: for edits to this doc's very long table rows specifically, verify the target line's real content with `sed -n '<n>p' file | wc -c` / `tail -c` before trusting anything `Read` displayed for that line, or just use `sed`/`awk` line-insertion (matching by line number, not string content) instead of `Edit`'s string-match — it sidesteps the truncation-mismatch problem entirely.** Minor self-inflicted follow-on: because one `Edit` call silently succeeded while a near-identical `sed` insert was also applied moments later (both aimed at the same D3 backlog row addition), the row was briefly duplicated — caught immediately via `grep -c` before committing, fixed with a single `sed -i '<n>d'`. Always `grep -c` a just-inserted unique marker (e.g. "SHIPPED (run N)") before committing a doc edit assembled from a mix of `Edit` and `sed` calls, to catch double-application.
- **All 5 dimension subagents (D1, D2, D3, D4, D5) completed cleanly on the first dispatch this run, zero stuck-background-wait incidents — worth noting as a data point against the "budget one resume per dispatch as the default" guidance from runs 26–39 (run 40):** Every subagent's dispatch prompt this run repeated the by-now-standard explicit instructions (redirect validate output to a worktree-local log, never pipe through `tail`, check exit code on the same line as the command, run validate/build synchronously in the foreground rather than backgrounding and ending the turn to wait). All 5 returned a genuine final report without needing a `SendMessage` resume. Sample size of one clean run doesn't override the accumulated 10+ prior runs' experience — continue budgeting for the stuck-wait failure mode as the expected case, not the exception — but it's plausible the by-now-very-explicit prompt language (evolved over 39 prior runs' worth of gotchas) is gradually reducing its frequency rather than it being purely random per-dispatch luck.
- **A new variant of the background-exit-code family: `nohup cmd > log 2>&1 & echo "started pid $!"` run via the harness's own `run_in_background: true` reports the WRAPPER shell's exit, not the backgrounded command's, because the wrapper itself returns instantly (run 39):** The orchestrator used this pattern twice this run (Phase 0 baseline `pnpm run validate`, and again independently re-verifying D3's branch before shipping) — both times the task-notification said "completed, exit code 0" within seconds, while `ps aux` showed the real `pnpm run validate`/`build` process (a different PID than the shell that launched it) still running minutes later. This is a distinct trap from the already-documented `echo "EXIT:$?"` and `| tail` pitfalls: here there's no trailing status-report command to misattribute — the _launcher itself_ is what returns immediately, because `nohup ... &` backgrounds the real work at the OS level and hands control back to the wrapping shell right away, and that wrapping shell is what the harness's `run_in_background` was actually tracking. **Takeaway: never treat a background-task "completed" notification as ground truth for a command you launched via `nohup ... &` (or any `&`-backgrounded pattern) inside a Bash call — after launching, immediately `ps aux | grep <command>` to find the REAL child PID (not the wrapper shell's), then background a separate `while kill -0 <real-pid>; do sleep 5; done` wait and treat only _that_ notification, plus the target log file's actual contents (grep for pass/fail markers, not just exit codes), as truth.** This worked cleanly both times once applied — the fix is mechanical, just easy to forget mid-routine.
- **A subagent's uncommitted diff can look "safe" in its own self-report yet be exactly the pattern a standing intentional exception exists to block — catch it via direct worktree inspection, not by trusting the eventual writeup (run 39):** D1's first attempt converted `ExpectationsWidget/Widget.tsx`'s "No expectation categories enabled for this building." — a text-only, no-icon state — to `ScaledEmptyState`, adding a `SlidersHorizontal` icon that wasn't there before. This is precisely the already-catalogued D1-E16 exception (same family as D1-E9/E15/E17/E23: converting a deliberately-spare no-icon state forces a new icon + `ScaledEmptyState`'s styling, a real visual change). The subagent never got to self-report this as a finished result — it hit the also-recurring stuck-background-wait failure mode first, which forced the orchestrator to inspect the worktree directly (per the established recovery pattern) _before_ the subagent could present its own "this looks clean" framing. That inspection is what caught the bad pick. Sent back with a specific citation of which exception it matched and why; the subagent reverted cleanly and searched again, finding nothing else fixable and correctly reporting "aligned" instead. **Takeaway, reinforcing the run-35 note below: don't wait for a subagent's own confidence signal before reviewing its diff — inspect the actual working tree yourself as soon as you have worktree access, whether that's during a stuck-agent recovery or a normal completion.** This is now the second time (run 35, run 39) an orchestrator diff-review caught a bad D1 pick specifically in a family of already-documented no-icon exceptions — worth double-checking any future D1 empty-state conversion against the no-icon exception family (D1-E9/E15/E16/E17/E23) by name before approving.
- **`cmd > log 2>&1; echo "EXIT:$?"` (or the same on two separate lines) reports the ECHO's exit code to the orchestrator's own background-task notification, not the underlying command's — this bit the orchestrator itself, not a subagent (run 37):** The orchestrator's own Phase-0 baseline `pnpm run validate` background call used this pattern; the task-notification summary reported "exit code 0" both times, but the first run's actual log showed a genuine test failure (`functions/src/googleOAuth.test.ts` — see flake note below) with `ELIFECYCLE Command failed with exit code 1`. The reported "0" was `echo`'s own always-succeeds exit status, not `pnpm run validate`'s — a background-command analogue of the already-documented `| tail` pitfall. Caught only because the orchestrator tailed the log file directly instead of trusting the notification summary. **Takeaway: never trust a background-task notification's reported exit code when the command line ends in a separate `echo`/status-report step — that echo's own exit status is what gets reported. Redirect the target command's own output to a file and grep/tail that file for pass/fail markers directly; don't rely on a trailing echo's exit code for anything.**
- **A second flaky-under-isolation test surfaced during the baseline validate — different file, same shape as the previously-documented `useRosters.test.ts` flake (run 37):** `functions/src/googleOAuth.test.ts`'s `revokeGoogleRefreshToken > deletes the doc and skips the Google call when the stored ciphertext is undecryptable` failed on the first baseline run (`expected true to be false`) but passed cleanly (4/4) when re-run in isolation immediately after, and passed again as part of a full clean re-run of `pnpm run validate` moments later (706/706 functions tests green). No dimension worktrees existed yet at the time of the first run (they were being created concurrently via `git worktree add`, a lightweight operation), so this wasn't the documented concurrent-`pnpm`-process CPU contention — more likely order-dependent test pollution within the same file/run. **Takeaway: a single baseline test failure is still not an automatic red-gate stop — always re-run the specific failing file in isolation, then re-run the full baseline once, before concluding the starting point is genuinely broken.** Worth flagging to a human if a 3rd distinct flaky test surfaces in a future run — two different files flaking under two different circumstances suggests a broader test-isolation issue worth a dedicated look, not just "always re-run once and move on" forever.
- **The `components/plc/**`ESLint regex vs.`PLC_SECTIONS` drift (recurred runs 28, 34, 2026-07-15) has now held clean for 3 consecutive checks (run 37):\*\* No action needed. Downgrading this from an active watch-item to routine-standard re-diff — still worth checking each D4 run, but no longer flagged as "likely to have drifted again."
- **Dispatch prompts that tell subagents to redirect validate output to a literal shared path (e.g. `/tmp/validate.log`) will collide the moment 2+ dimension worktrees run concurrently — always use a worktree-scoped or dimension-scoped log path (run 36):** This run's dispatch prompts suggested `pnpm run validate > /tmp/validate.log 2>&1` verbatim to every subagent. Two independent subagents (D3 and D4) discovered mid-run that this exact path was being clobbered by sibling dimension worktrees' own validate runs writing to the same file simultaneously — one subagent's first attempt showed a misleadingly "successful" exit code that actually belonged to a different worktree's run. Both self-corrected by redirecting to a worktree-local path instead (e.g. `<worktree>/validate.log` or a scratchpad file named per-dimension) before trusting the result. **Takeaway: future dispatch prompts should never suggest a bare `/tmp/<name>.log` path for a command a subagent will run inside its own worktree — always suggest a path scoped to the worktree itself (`$(pwd)/validate.log`) or explicitly per-dimension-named, since multiple worktrees' agents run concurrently by design in this routine.**
- **The stuck-background-wait subagent failure mode recurred again (1 of 5 dispatches, D3) despite the by-now-standard explicit foreground-execution instruction — this remains the routine's single most reliable recurring cost, not an outlier (run 36):** D3's subagent correctly found and committed a clean, correct fix, then ended its turn saying it had a Monitor watching for its own backgrounded validate run to finish — the same failure shape documented in every run's notes since run 26. Recovery technique held again: the orchestrator inspected the worktree directly first (confirmed the diff was correct AND the validate process was genuinely still running, not stuck/dead, via `ps aux` + tailing its log), then resumed via `SendMessage` with both a specific grounded observation ("your diff looks right, useId() is the correct call here") and an explicit "block synchronously, poll for your own process, do not end your turn waiting again" instruction. Completed cleanly on the first resume, consistent with every prior run's experience of this exact recovery pattern. **Takeaway, now confirmed 10+ runs running: continue budgeting one resume per dispatch as the expected cost of this routine, not an exception.**
- **All 5 dimension worktrees created manually (skip `isolation: worktree`) and symlinked from a single verified-fresh `origin/dev-paul` fetch worked cleanly 5-for-5 with zero staleness incidents this run (run 36):** Following the run-28/29 recommendation, all 5 worktrees were cut directly (`git worktree add -B nightly/unify-<dim>-2026-07-17 <path> origin/dev-paul`) from one orchestrator-verified `git fetch` immediately before dispatch, with `node_modules`/`functions/node_modules` symlinked in and plain `general-purpose` agents pointed at the pre-built paths (no `isolation: worktree`). Zero worktree-staleness incidents, zero lost-worktree incidents — reinforces continuing to skip `isolation: worktree` for dimension dispatch entirely.
- **A dispatched subagent's "clean, unambiguous" conversion can still match an established exception shape it wasn't primed to recognize — always diff-review before trusting a self-assessment (run 35):** D1's subagent (and its own nested grep-sweep sub-agent) both assessed `QuizEditor.tsx:191`'s "No questions yet" conversion as safe, but the original was a text-only, no-icon state — the exact shape the D1-E9/E15/E16/E17 exceptions exist to protect (converting adds a new icon + forces `ScaledEmptyState`'s hardcoded uppercase title casing). The subagent's dispatch prompt _did_ explicitly warn about this shape, but it still missed the match until the orchestrator's independent diff review caught it and cited the precedent directly — the subagent then agreed and self-corrected immediately. Its own nested sweep agent separately recommended `ActivityWall/Widget.tsx:1561` as "clean," which is actually a well-known, multi-run VISUAL-RISK backlog item — the sweep agent had no exceptions/backlog context at all. **Takeaway: read the actual diff yourself before accepting a subagent's "this one's safe" self-assessment, even when the dispatch prompt named the relevant exception family explicitly — and never let a subagent's own nested sweep-agent recommendation substitute for orchestrator review, since nested agents typically lack the full backlog/exceptions context.** Silver lining: once the orchestrator's diff review DID surface a real fix for the ActivityWall item (a scoped `container-type: size` boundary, verified against 4 existing codebase precedents), it resolved a VISUAL-RISK item that had been sitting untouched since run 26 — so the same diff-review discipline that catches a bad conversion can also validate a genuinely good one instead of reflexively rejecting anything flagged risky.
- **Piping a validate run through `tail` silently discards the real exit code — a subagent flagged this about its own work, and the orchestrator independently re-verified by redirecting to a file instead (run 35):** `pnpm run validate | tail -N` reports `tail`'s exit status in a bash pipeline (no `pipefail`), not the underlying command's — a background validate run backgrounded via this pattern can show "exit code 0" even if validate itself failed. The orchestrator's own Phase-0 baseline check hit this same pattern; it was fine because the tail output showed the final chained step (`test:counts`) succeeding, which only happens if every earlier `&&`-chained step also passed — but that's a fragile way to confirm success. For any validate run whose trustworthiness matters (e.g. re-verifying a subagent's claim), redirect to a real file (`pnpm run validate > file.log 2>&1; echo $?`) instead of piping through `tail`.
- **The `components/plc/**`ESLint regex vs.`PLC_SECTIONS`drift has now recurred 3 times (runs 28, 34, 2026-07-15) and held clean on the 4th check (run 35) — this is worth fixing at the root rather than continuing to re-diff by eye every night:** A D4 subagent proposed deriving the regex programmatically from`PLC_SECTIONS`at lint/build time (e.g. a`tests/rules`-style unit test that imports the array and asserts every id appears in the `eslint.config.js`string), rather than relying on a human/agent re-diff each run. Logged here as a standing proposal for whoever next touches`eslint.config.js`'s plc rule — not implemented this run (D4 had nothing to ship, the regex held).
- **The stuck-background-wait subagent failure mode hit 3 of 5 dispatches yet again this run (D1, D3, D4), despite the same explicit foreground-execution instruction baked into every dispatch prompt — this is now a near-certain per-run tax, budget for it (run 34):** Consistent with runs 26–33's notes below. All 3 stuck agents had genuine, verifiable in-progress work when the orchestrator inspected their worktrees directly (`git status`/`git diff origin/dev-paul --stat`, `ps aux` showing a real lingering `tsc`/`eslint`/`vitest` process under the worktree's own path) — none had silently died or lost work. The recovery technique from prior runs continued to work 3/3: `SendMessage` with an explicit "find your own PID via ps aux, block on it in the foreground (`while kill -0 <PID>; do sleep 5; done` or just re-run the command fresh), do not background-and-stop again" instruction got all 3 to a genuine completed result on the first resume, no repeat stalls. **Refinement this run:** the orchestrator inspected each stuck agent's worktree (diff + running processes) _before_ composing the resume message, and fed back a specific, worktree-grounded observation (e.g. "your diff looks good, useId() is the right call here") alongside the resume instruction — this seemed to help the agent finish decisively rather than re-second-guessing its own work after being unstuck. **Takeaway, now repeated 6+ runs running: stop treating this as an occasional recovery and start budgeting one resume per shipping dimension (D1/D3/D4-style dimensions that actually run validate+build) as the default expected cost of every dispatch, not an exception path.**
- **Independently re-verifying a subagent's "sibling file precedent" claim is worth the extra few minutes — it turned a plausible-sounding safety argument into an actually-confirmed one (run 34):** D1's QuizManager.tsx conversion cited `VideoActivityManager.tsx:1007` as a "direct precedent" for using bare (no color-override) `ScaledEmptyState` inside `LibraryShell`. The orchestrator's independent review noticed `LibraryShell`'s root sets `text-slate-800` (a light-surface signal, structurally similar to the run-30 `ExpectationsWidget` light-surface trap that fooled both a subagent and one automated reviewer) and actually opened `VideoActivityManager.tsx` to confirm the cited line, rather than trusting the citation. It checked out exactly as claimed — same `LibraryShell` wrapper, same bare `ScaledEmptyState`, already shipped and merged. A same-shape concern was independently raised by `claude[bot]`'s automated review on PR #2206 (color mismatch between `ScaledEmptyState`'s light-on-dark defaults and `LibraryShell`'s `bg-white/60` chrome) and reached the identical "matches existing precedent, not a new regression, but worth a follow-up pass" conclusion. **Takeaway: "a sibling file already does this" is a claim to verify by opening the sibling file, not evidence to accept at face value — it's cheap to check and the ExpectationsWidget incident shows it can be wrong.** **New backlog item surfaced by this cross-check (not acted on):** both `QuizManager.tsx`'s and `VideoActivityManager.tsx`'s active/archive `ScaledEmptyState` calls render `ScaledEmptyState`'s light-on-dark default text colors (`text-slate-200/300`) against `LibraryShell`'s `bg-white/60`/`bg-white/40` translucent-white chrome — plausibly a pre-existing (not newly-introduced) low-contrast issue affecting both widgets equally. Worth a dedicated future pass to thread theme-aware `titleClassName`/`subtitleClassName` overrides through both managers' `LibraryShell`-hosted empty states, verified with an actual rendered screenshot/contrast check (per the run-30 `ScaledEmptyState`-defaults gotcha below), not just code reading.
- **A second occurrence of the "enforcement regex drifts behind its own source of truth" bug class — worth a standing watch-item, not just a one-off fix (run 34):** D4's `eslint.config.js` `components/plc/**` regex (added run 28, meant to track every id in `components/plc/sections.ts`'s `PLC_SECTIONS` array so a relative import into a not-yet-created section directory is still caught) was missing `assessments` and `todos` — both real, currently-used `PLC_SECTIONS` ids. This is the _second_ time this exact drift has been found (the first was run 28's own missing `members`/`sharedBoards`, caught by `gemini-code-assist` post-merge). **Takeaway: a forward-looking enforcement regex that mirrors a separate source-of-truth array needs to be re-diffed against that array periodically, not just written once and trusted — add "re-diff the plc regex against `PLC_SECTIONS`" to the standard D4 dispatch checklist rather than waiting for a 3rd recurrence.**
- **D5's "renders behind the modal" exception rationale may no longer hold — flagged for human review, not acted on (run 33):** A D5 subagent traced the actual DOM/stacking-context chain and z-index registry (`config/zIndex.ts`: `toast: 14000` vs `modal: 10000`/`modalNested: 10100`/`modalDeep: 10200`) and found that the long-standing rationale behind ~10 catalogued D5 exceptions (`FeaturePermissionsManager.tsx`, `BackgroundManager/index.tsx`, `GlobalPermissionsManager.tsx`, the `*ConfigurationModal.tsx`/`*LibraryModal.tsx` family — "global `addToast`'s `ToastContainer` would render behind the modal's z-index") appears to contradict the current numeric z-index ordering: `toast` (14000) is higher than every modal tier. If correct, `addToast()` should already render above these modals, not behind them — meaning the premise for treating these as intentional exceptions may be stale, not that the exceptions are wrong per se. Deliberately NOT converted this run: 10+ files is far beyond a single-instance nightly diff, and CSS stacking-context edge cases (backdrop-filter, `position: fixed` containing blocks) need a live-browser check, not just static reasoning, before touching this much toast plumbing unattended. **Takeaway: schedule a dedicated, human-reviewed, browser-verified D5 pass to re-examine whether these ~10 exception files should actually move to `addToast()`** — do not silently convert them on a future run's static-analysis say-so alone, and do not silently continue treating them as settled either.
- **The stuck-background-wait subagent failure mode hit 4 of 5 dispatches this run (D1, D3, D4, D5) despite an explicit "run synchronously in the foreground, don't background validate/build and end your turn waiting" instruction baked directly into every dispatch prompt (run 33):** D1 backgrounded a research/search sub-agent and stopped; D3 and D5 each backgrounded `pnpm run validate`/an audit agent and stopped; D4 was outright killed after running 9+ minutes stuck waiting on a backgrounded full-repo `eslint --max-warnings 0`. All four were recovered by the orchestrator resuming them via `SendMessage` with an explicit "check on your background process, wait for it synchronously within this turn, do not spawn another background wait" instruction — this worked every time, including on the killed D4 agent (resumable via SendMessage even from a `killed` status, not just `completed`). **Takeaway: this is now the dominant failure mode in this routine (4/5 dispatches, not an outlier) — the dispatch-prompt instruction alone is not sufficient to prevent it, but the SendMessage-resume recovery is reliable. Budget for at least one resume per subagent as the expected case, not an exception. If a future orchestrator wants to reduce this further, consider explicitly telling subagents which specific commands are safe to run at full duration in the foreground (validate/build/full-repo-lint can legitimately take minutes) versus explicitly forbidding the `run_in_background`-style tool option for those commands.**
- **A same-session baseline validate can silently check the WRONG file version if you edit-then-revert a file while the validate process is still running (run 33):** The orchestrator applied a local fix to `docs/routines/unifier.md` (deduplicating corrupted content), then discovered an open sibling PR (#2187) already fixed it more thoroughly, and reverted its own local edit via `git checkout --` — but had already kicked off the baseline `pnpm run validate` in the background moments earlier, while its own (clean) locally-fixed doc was still on disk. Because `format:check` (prettier) runs partway through the validate chain, and the revert happened within the first minute (well before `format:check` would normally execute), it's likely the timing worked out fine as a race — but this was never verified directly, and the ambiguity was only caught later when 3 independent dimension subagents in fresh worktrees (which never had the local fix) all independently reported that `prettier --check docs/routines/unifier.md` genuinely fails on the true current `dev-paul` HEAD. **Takeaway: never edit a file (even to "just check something") after kicking off a background validate run you intend to treat as your baseline — the check may silently run against a transient, uncommitted state rather than the actual committed tree. If you must investigate/revert a file mid-validate, re-run the baseline check (or at least the specific affected sub-step) after the working tree has settled, not before.** Practical resolution this run: treated the doc-file format:check failure as a known, already-diagnosed, already-being-fixed (open PR #2187) pre-existing issue unrelated to any of this run's actual code changes — not a reason to halt the whole routine — and noted it explicitly in every shipped PR's description so CI's expected red doesn't get mistaken for a regression.

- **Group-heading `SettingsLabel` retrofits need a per-instance-scoped `id` when the host component isn't a modal singleton — a real bug caught post-PR by `claude[bot]` review, not by validate/build (run 32):** The first three `as="span"` group-heading conversions (runs 26/29/30 — `MagicLayoutModal.tsx`, `InstructionalRoutines/LibraryManager.tsx`, `MiniApp/components/SaveAsWidgetModal.tsx`) all live inside modal singletons, so a hardcoded static `id` string was safe (only ever one instance in the DOM). Run 32's `DrawingWidget/Settings.tsx` "Color Presets" conversion used the same hardcoded-`id` pattern, but `DrawingSettings` renders per-widget-instance inside `DraggableWindow` — with 2+ DrawingWidgets on a dashboard both flipped to settings, the static `id="drawing-color-presets-label"` would produce duplicate DOM ids (invalid HTML) and make `aria-labelledby` unreliable. `pnpm run validate`/`build` cannot catch this (it's a multi-instance DOM-uniqueness issue, not a type/lint/test failure) — it was caught by an automated PR review (`claude[bot]`) after the PR was already open. Fixed by scoping the id to the widget instance (``id={\`drawing-color-presets-label-${widget.id}\`}``). **Takeaway for future D3 group-heading retrofits: before hardcoding a static `id` string, check whether the target component is a modal singleton (safe) or renders per-widget-instance/per-list-item (needs the id scoped by `widget.id` or an equivalent instance key) — grep the component for how many times it can mount concurrently before assuming a bare string id is safe.**
- **Doc-duplication near-miss averted by cross-checking the code-fix branch's base against the actual current doc state, not just `dev-paul` (run 32):** The D4 subagent's dispatch prompt didn't explicitly forbid touching `docs/routines/unifier.md`, and it edited the file as part of its commit — based on its worktree's `dev-paul` checkout (run-30 content), not the actual current state (the still-unmerged run-31 doc branch this run built on top of). Had that edit shipped as-is in the PR, merging it would have silently reverted the run-31 doc content back to run-30's, then this run's separate doc-update PR would have landed on top and diverged — a variant of the exact run-22/run-29 duplication failure mode already documented below, just introduced via a code PR instead of two competing doc PRs. Caught by the orchestrator reviewing the D4 branch's diff before opening its PR; fixed by reverting just the doc file on that branch (new commit, not amend) before pushing. **Takeaway: dimension dispatch prompts should default to "do not touch docs/routines/unifier.md — the orchestrator handles all doc updates centrally in Phase 4" unless a run explicitly delegates doc-writing to a subagent; and the orchestrator must diff every shipped branch's full file list (not just the files named in the subagent's own report) before opening a PR, since a subagent may touch files it wasn't asked to.**
- **Stale-backlog-row hygiene: run 30 formalized 4 D1 NEEDS-REVIEW items as exceptions (D1-E19–E22) but never updated their backlog table rows, leaving them looking like open work (run 31):** The D1 Inconsistency Backlog table still listed `QuizLiveMonitor.tsx:2887`, `GuidedLearningResults.tsx:331`, `PersonalSpotifyNowPlayingTab.tsx:65`, and `VideoActivityEditor.tsx:393` as `NEEDS REVIEW` even though run 30's Run Log entry and the Intentional Exceptions table both already closed them out as D1-E19 through D1-E22. A future dispatch reading only the backlog table (not cross-referencing the exceptions table) could have wasted a turn re-investigating already-decided items. Fixed in run 31's doc pass — all 4 rows now read `CLOSED (D1-Enn)`. **Takeaway: when formalizing a NEEDS-REVIEW backlog item as an exception in the same run, update both tables in the same edit** — the exceptions table alone isn't enough if the backlog table still shows it as open.
- **The stuck-background-wait subagent failure mode hit again (1 of 5 dispatches, D4) even with explicit foreground-execution instructions (run 31):** Consistent with runs 26–30 — this remains a persistent, not occasional, failure mode. This time the orchestrator's fix was refined slightly: rather than immediately re-running `pnpm run validate` from scratch (which would contend with the stuck agent's own still-running `tsc --noEmit` process for CPU, risking the documented concurrent-worktree flake), the orchestrator first checked for and waited on the specific lingering PID (`kill -0 <pid>` poll loop) before starting its own validate run in that worktree. Zero flakes, clean single-pass green. **Refinement for future runs: before launching a fresh validate/build in a worktree recovered from a stuck agent, `ps aux | grep -E "vitest|eslint|tsc|vite build"` first — if the agent's own command is still running, wait for it to exit rather than doubling up.**
- **`i18n/index.ts` was a previously-unswept D4 target — the repo's root-level "misc" files (not inside `components/`, `context/`, `hooks/`, `utils/`, `config/`, `tests/`) are worth an explicit periodic check (run 31):** 30 prior runs swept every major directory but never explicitly targeted `i18n/index.ts`, which had 4 relative imports (`'../locales/*.json'`) reaching from the root-level `i18n/` directory into the sibling root-level `locales/` directory — a clean, unambiguous instance of the D4 anti-pattern, just sitting in a directory no prior dispatch prompt happened to name. Fixed in PR #2174 (mechanical, zero enforcement needed — isolated single file). **Takeaway: periodically grep the whole repo root (not just the directories explicitly named in past run logs) for cross-directory relative imports — new "misc small directory" targets can hide indefinitely if every dispatch prompt only lists previously-known directories.**
- **D3 candidate future dimension: audit pre-existing `<SettingsLabel>` (default `as="label"`) usages that head a group of controls rather than pairing 1:1, for retrofit to `as="span"` (surfaced run 31, not investigated in depth):** The `as="span"` group-heading variant (added outside this routine, PR #2141, formalized as canon in run 30) has so far only been applied to the 3 instances that were newly converted from raw hand-rolled HTML in runs 26/29. The much larger population of `<SettingsLabel>` call sites that predate PR #2141 and already head a group of sibling controls (e.g. `DrawingWidget/Settings.tsx` "Color Presets", `RevealGrid/Settings.tsx` "Columns", `random/RandomSettings.tsx` "Animation Style", `MusicWidget/Settings.tsx` "Layout" — dozens more per a preliminary D3 grep) have never been retrofitted and still render an orphaned `<label>`. This is plausibly a large, multi-run D3 dimension of its own (semantics-only, zero visual delta, same shape as the run-30 retrofit) — flagged here for a future run to scope and dispatch explicitly, rather than folding it into a routine single-instance D3 dispatch.
- **The run-22 doc-duplication failure mode recurred a 2nd time, across sessions this time — and the clean recovery technique is worth keeping (run 30):** The still-open run-29 doc branch (`nightly/unifier-log-2026-07-08`, PR #2165) had accumulated a stray "Merge branch 'dev-paul' into ..." commit (apparently an automated mergeability-check side effect, not anything this routine did deliberately) that duplicated the entire run-28 Run Log rows and Notes entries — byte-for-byte the same symptom as the run-22 incident (295KB bloat) documented below. **Recovery technique that worked cleanly:** confirmed the unifier branch's own pre-corruption run-28 doc content was byte-identical to `dev-paul`'s already-merged run-28 doc (`git diff <unifier-branch-run28-sha> <dev-paul-sha> -- docs/routines/unifier.md` was empty) — meaning the two branches never actually diverged on run 28, so extracting the run-29-_only_ delta (`git diff <run28-sha> <run29-tip-sha>`) and cleanly re-applying it on top of current `dev-paul` via `git apply` was a mechanical, zero-loss reconciliation, no manual dedup needed. This only works when the two "copies" being merged are actually identical; if they'd diverged (e.g. two sessions both wrote different run-28 content), a manual side-by-side dedup would be required instead. **Going forward:** when adopting an open sibling doc branch's tip per the run-27 protocol, always sanity-check it hasn't accumulated a stray merge before building on it — `git log --oneline -- docs/routines/unifier.md` on the branch should show a straight line of `docs(unifier): log nightly run N` commits, not a "Merge branch 'dev-paul' into ..." commit partway through.
- **`ScaledEmptyState`'s default text colors assume a dark widget surface — verify the target widget's own established palette before converting, don't trust the component's defaults blindly (run 30, PR #2167 review):** `ScaledEmptyState`'s own doc comment says "defaults are slate tones for dark widgets" (`text-slate-200`/`text-slate-300`), consistent with the app's general dark-slate-900-dashboard convention. But `ExpectationsWidget` is one of a small number of genuinely **light-surface** widgets (`bg-white` buttons, `text-slate-800` headers, `text-slate-500` body text throughout, transparent root with no dark card wrapper) — converting its hand-rolled empty state to `ScaledEmptyState` with no overrides would have made the empty-state text nearly invisible against a light backdrop, a real regression the D1 subagent and one automated reviewer (`claude[bot]`) both missed by assuming "dark surface" as the default without checking this widget's actual surrounding styles; a second automated reviewer (`gemini-code-assist`) caught it. Fixed via `iconClassName`/`titleClassName`/`subtitleClassName` overrides matching the widget's own established tokens (`text-slate-500`/`text-slate-800`/`text-slate-500`) rather than gemini's suggested values verbatim, for internal consistency with the widget's other headers/body text. **Before any future D1 conversion, grep the target widget file for its own `bg-white`/`text-slate-800`+ prevalence before assuming the app-wide dark-dashboard default applies — a handful of widgets (light-surface UI patterns, admin-adjacent widgets) don't follow it.**
- **`SettingsLabel` gained an `as="span"` group-heading variant outside this routine, resolving the run-26 architecture question (discovered run 30):** A separate PR (#2141 review-fix pass, commit `558dd3e`) added `as?: 'label' | 'span'` + `id?: string` to `components/common/SettingsLabel.tsx` and retrofitted 4 admin library modals to use it (`MiniAppLibraryModal.tsx`, `PdfLibraryModal.tsx`, `StickerLibraryModal.tsx`, `WorkSymbolsConfigurationModal.tsx`) — the fix the run-26 note below said would need "a cross-cutting change touching 154 call sites, well beyond a single nightly PR's blast radius." It didn't touch the other 150 call sites (those remain `as="label"`, which is correct for 1:1-paired labels) — only the group-heading shape needed the new variant. This run retrofitted the 3 known orphaned-label instances from run 26 (PR #2144: `MagicLayoutModal.tsx`, `LibraryManager.tsx`, `SaveAsWidgetModal.tsx`) to match. **The run-26 "needs human decision" framing is now resolved** — `as="span"` + `role="group"`/`aria-labelledby` is the canonical fix for group headings; update future D3 dispatch prompts to check for this shape (a `SettingsLabel` heading a `flex`/`grid` of multiple sibling interactive controls with no single associated control) as a routine conversion target, not a standing exception.
- **`dev-paul` can move mid-run even after a green baseline validate — always re-fetch before pushing, and expect to rebase (run 30):** Between kicking off this run's baseline `pnpm run validate` and opening PRs ~40 minutes later, `dev-paul` advanced twice (3 unrelated PRs merged: #2155/#2156/#2157, then #2164/#2166) while the 5 dimension subagents worked in their pinned-at-dispatch-time worktrees. This is expected — other routines and humans push to `dev-paul` independently — but it means the "cut all worktrees from one fresh HEAD, dispatch, done" flow from a same-run-in-one-shot session is optimistic; budget for at least one rebase-revalidate-rebuild cycle per branch before opening PRs even when nothing went wrong dimension-side. Sequential rebase + full revalidate + rebuild on all 3 shipped branches this run added ~15 minutes but caught zero real conflicts (clean rebases throughout) — cheap insurance, always do it, per the existing Phase 3 instruction.
- **The stuck-background-wait subagent failure mode hit 2 of 5 dispatches again this run (D3, D4) despite explicit "run in the foreground, don't end your turn waiting" instructions in the dispatch prompt (run 30):** Confirms this is a persistent, not occasional, failure mode (see runs 26/27/28 notes below) — explicit prompt instructions alone don't reliably prevent it. The orchestrator inspecting the worktree directly (`git status`/`git diff`, then independently running `pnpm run validate`/`build` itself rather than resuming the stuck agent) continues to be the reliable fix, and is now the default assumption going in, not a fallback: **budget orchestrator time for directly finishing 1-2 of the 5 dispatches' validate/build/commit/push steps every run**, rather than expecting all 5 subagents to self-complete.
- **CSS margin collapsing does NOT apply between a `SettingsLabel` and the form control below it when that control is `<textarea>`, `<input>`, `<select>`, or `<button>` — verify empirically, don't reason from memory (run 29, PR #2164 review):** When converting a hand-rolled label to `<SettingsLabel>` (which adds `block mb-2`) sitting directly above one of these form controls inside a `space-y-*` container, the intuitive "adjacent block-level margins collapse, net gap unchanged" reasoning is wrong — these elements' UA-stylesheet default `display` is `inline-block`, not `block`, and margin collapsing only applies between adjacent **block-level** boxes. The label's `mb-2` and the control's `space-y-*`-derived `margin-top` are additive, not collapsing (confirmed empirically via a real Chromium/Playwright `getBoundingClientRect()` measurement: 8px + 8px → 16px gap, not 8px). This is a real, if minor, visual change on every such conversion, not a preserved one — judge it against the established "mb-1→mb-2 canonical alignment" precedent (accepted in PRs #1783/#1870) rather than claiming equivalence in the PR description. **When behavior-preservation is claimed based on CSS box-model reasoning (margin collapse, specificity, etc.), verify it with an actual rendered measurement (a scratch Playwright script, or compiled Tailwind CSS as run 25 did) before asserting it in a PR description — "adjacent margins collapse" is not true unconditionally, and getting it wrong undermines every other behavior-preservation claim in the same write-up.**
- **Manual-worktree-from-the-start (skip `isolation:worktree` entirely) worked cleanly all 5-for-5 this run (run 29):** Following run 28's recommendation, all 5 dimension worktrees were created directly by the orchestrator (`git worktree add -B nightly/unify-<dim>-2026-07-08 <path> dev-paul`) up front, before any dispatch, with `node_modules`/`functions/node_modules` symlinked in and plain `general-purpose` agents (no `isolation:worktree`) pointed at the pre-built paths. Every one of the 5 subagents confirmed freshness (`git merge-base HEAD origin/dev-paul` == `origin/dev-paul` HEAD) and completed without a single staleness or background-wait-stall incident — a clean run, unlike runs 24/25/27/28 which each hit at least one. Reinforces run 28's recommendation: **default to this pattern, skip `isolation:worktree` for dimension dispatch entirely** until the underlying harness bug is fixed.
- **Baseline `pnpm run validate` can flake under the same concurrent-worktree CPU contention the debugger routine already documented (run 29):** Running the orchestrator's baseline `validate` on the main checkout at the same time as 5 dimension subagents were running their own `validate`/`build`/lint passes in sibling worktrees caused `tests/hooks/useRosters.test.ts`'s PII-migration test to fail once (`TypeError: Cannot read properties of undefined (reading 'students')`). Re-running that one file in isolation immediately afterward passed 35/35. This is the same flake the debugger routine's PR #2159 body independently documented ("seen under concurrent-worktree CPU contention... confirmed unrelated... passes in isolation and on a clean re-run") — cross-routine confirmation it's a resource-contention flake, not a real regression. **Do not treat a single-test failure in the baseline validate as a red gate without first re-running that file in isolation**, especially when dimension worktrees are about to run (or are already running) their own heavy `pnpm` commands concurrently.
- **Coordinating with a same-night sibling automated routine's open PRs, not just this routine's own (run 29):** At Phase 0, `list_pull_requests` surfaced 9 open PRs against `dev-paul`, only 2 of which (`#2155`, `#2156`) belonged to this unifier routine — the other 7 belonged to a separate "nightly debugger" routine (`nightly/debugger-log-2026-07-07` plus 5 sibling bugfix PRs, and one `scheduled-tasks` skill-freshness PR). None touched files this run's dimensions modified, so no action was needed beyond noting them, but the general lesson generalizes past the run-27 "check for open unifier-log PRs" note: **check ALL open PRs against the base branch at Phase 0, not just ones matching this routine's own branch-naming convention** — a different automated routine's in-flight work could plausibly collide on shared files (e.g. both routines touching the same widget) even though this run didn't hit that case.
- **Manually-created worktrees are a reliable workaround for the recurring `isolation: worktree` staleness bug (run 28):** Of 5 dimension subagents dispatched via the Agent tool's `isolation: "worktree"` option, 3 (D1, D2, D4) were cut from a stale base — `git merge-base HEAD origin/dev-paul` resolved to a commit 44 commits behind the real `origin/dev-paul` tip. D2 and D4 self-detected this (per their dispatch instructions to verify before proceeding) and correctly stopped without doing any work. D5's worktree was fresh and completed normally — confirming again (as in runs 24/25/27) that the staleness is per-worktree-creation, not a global clock/cache issue, so it cannot be assumed away for any given dispatch. **Fix used this run:** the orchestrator manually created worktrees directly (`git worktree add -B nightly/unify-<dim>-<date> <path> origin/dev-paul`) from its own already-verified-current checkout, symlinked `node_modules`/`functions/node_modules` into each, and redispatched plain `general-purpose` agents (no `isolation: worktree`) with explicit `cd <path>` instructions instead of letting the harness provision the worktree. All 4 redispatches (D1, D2, D3, D4) then verified clean against the real `origin/dev-paul` tip and produced usable results. **Recommendation for future runs:** default to this manual-worktree pattern for dimension dispatch rather than `isolation: worktree`, at least until the underlying cached/pinned-snapshot bug (suspected across runs 24, 25, 27, 28) is fixed at the infra level.
- **A subagent that ends its turn mid-background-wait can lose its own harness-managed worktree entirely, not just "go stale" (run 28):** D1 and D3's original dispatches (both `isolation: worktree`) got stuck backgrounding `pnpm run validate` and ending their turn saying some version of "I'll pause and wait for the notification" — the same failure mode runs 26/27 documented. This time, when the orchestrator went to inspect their worktrees to extract any in-progress work, `git worktree list` showed the D3 one already gone entirely (auto-cleaned, presumably because the harness saw no committed changes) and the D1 one still present but at the same stale 44-commits-behind base as D2/D4. **Net effect: any uncommitted progress those two agents had made was unrecoverable — extract-and-reapply (the established fix from runs 24/25) only works if the worktree still exists.** Fix: redispatch fresh into a manually-created worktree (see note above) rather than trying to resume/salvage. Also: when resuming a stuck agent via `SendMessage` instead of redispatching fresh (used for D4 this run, since its worktree was still present and not stale), explicitly tell it "do not background and wait — block synchronously, re-run the command in the foreground" — this successfully got D4 to completion on the second try without losing its already-fixed diff.
- **A subagent working in a fresh manually-created worktree found and reverted a stray uncommitted edit, attributing it to "a prior stuck attempt" (run 28):** The D1 retry, immediately after `cd`-ing into the freshly `git worktree add`-created path, reported finding an uncommitted change already sitting in `QuizWidget/Widget.tsx` and described it as leftover from the earlier stuck attempt. The orchestrator could not confirm a mechanism for this (the manual worktree was freshly cut from `origin/dev-paul` moments before dispatch, and no other process had touched that specific path in between) — the more likely explanation is the agent made its own exploratory edit early in its own session (prototyping the conversion), then reconsidered given the D1-E4 analogy and reverted it, but described the sequence using the "prior attempt" framing it had been primed with in its dispatch prompt. Either way it self-corrected correctly and the final state was clean. **Takeaway:** when a dispatch prompt tells an agent "a prior attempt failed and left X state," the agent may misattribute its own mid-task changes to that framing when reporting back — read git history/reflog rather than trusting the narrative if precision matters.
- **D3-E7/E8 ("lighter-weight `font-bold`-not-`font-black`" tier) is far more pervasive than its 2 named example files (run 28):** A fresh repo-wide grep for the exact canonical string turned up nothing new to convert, but incidentally surfaced ~20 additional files sharing the same `text-xxs font-bold text-slate-400 uppercase tracking-widest` weight-variant already covered by D3-E7/E8's rationale: `GenericConfigurationModal.tsx:67`, `CalendarConfigurationModal.tsx:299`, `SettingsPanel.tsx:318`, `AssignModal.tsx:147`, `UniversalStyleSettings.tsx:48,98,144`, `WidgetLibrary.tsx:311,393,461`, `SidebarGoogleDrive.tsx:176`, `RosterEditorModal.tsx:319`, `VideoActivityWidget/components/Creator.tsx:282,296`, `LinkSchoologyModal.tsx:191`, `AssignToClassroomModal.tsx:314`, `CollectionColorPicker.tsx:127,158`, `CheatSheetModal.tsx:215,239`, `QuickAccessModal.tsx:75`, `StationEditor.tsx:106,119,135,155,185`. None converted (converting would add `font-black`, a real visual-weight change) — noted here so a future doc pass can broaden D3-E7/E8's example list without re-discovering this from scratch.
- **gemini-code-assist PR review caught a real gap in a same-night enforcement rule — automated review is still useful even on nightly-routine PRs (run 28):** D4's new ESLint `no-restricted-imports` regex enumerated PLC subdirectory names but missed two canonical section IDs (`members`, `sharedBoards`) that exist in `components/plc/sections.ts` but don't have a directory yet. gemini-code-assist flagged this on PR #2155; verified the claim directly against `sections.ts` before applying it (both IDs are real, confirmed no existing directory or import references them yet, so the fix is pure forward-proofing). Applied the suggested regex widening. **Takeaway:** when adding enforcement for a bug class, cross-check the enumerated pattern against the schema/source-of-truth the pattern is meant to protect (here, `sections.ts`'s canonical `PlcSectionId` union), not just the directories that happen to exist today.

- **Two unmerged "run 26" nightly-log PRs existed simultaneously — check for open sibling doc PRs before writing a new one (run 27):** This run's dispatch read `docs/routines/unifier.md` as merged in `dev-paul` (still at run 25, since the previous night's doc PR hadn't been merged yet) and independently produced its own "run 26" — colliding in run number, and in two exception IDs (D2-E15, and a near-duplicate of the `SaveAsWidgetModal.tsx:100` D3 finding) with the actually-still-open `nightly/unifier-log-2026-07-05` PR (#2145, plus its sibling code PRs #2142/#2143/#2144). Caught via an automated PR review comment flagging "coordinate the two open run-26 unifier-log PRs." Fix applied: rebased this run's doc branch onto `nightly/unifier-log-2026-07-05`'s tip instead of `dev-paul`, renumbered as run 27, deduplicated the colliding exception entries (kept the more complete/evidence-backed version of each), and renumbered the free-standing D3-E19 conflict to D3-E20-candidate. **Going forward: before starting Phase 0, check open PRs for an existing `nightly/unifier-log-*` branch that hasn't merged yet — if one exists, treat its tip (not `dev-paul`) as the current doc state, and read it for backlog/canon context too, not just to avoid a numbering collision.** This is the same root failure mode as the run-22 duplication incident, just across sessions instead of within one.
- **`SettingsLabel` always renders `<label>`, even when there's no associated control — a repo-wide characteristic, not a per-PR regression (run 26, needs human decision):** Automated review on PR #2144 flagged 3 conversions (`MagicLayoutModal.tsx` "Try these" above sibling buttons, `LibraryManager.tsx` "Default Steps" above a list, `SaveAsWidgetModal.tsx` "Preview" above display text) for using `<label>` — which the component's own doc comment justifies via "implicit nesting-based association with any contained input" — with no contained/paired input at all. Checked the scale: **154 total `<SettingsLabel>` usages repo-wide, only 6 pass `htmlFor`.** The other 148 (96%) are this exact same bare-section-heading shape, shipped across 25+ prior runs — this is `SettingsLabel`'s dominant, established usage pattern, not something these 3 new instances introduced. A real fix would mean changing the shared component itself (e.g. render `<label>` only when `htmlFor` is passed or a control is nested, `<span>`/`<div>` otherwise) — a cross-cutting change touching 154 call sites, well beyond a single nightly PR's blast radius. **Needs a human decision**: is an orphaned `<label>` an acceptable tradeoff for this app (arguably low real-world impact — modern screen readers generally just read the text), or should `SettingsLabel` gain a conditional/`as` prop for the no-control case? Until decided, do not treat this as an actionable D3 backlog item — it's an architecture question, not a snowflake to unify.
- **`ScaledEmptyState` conversions inside a nested sub-panel need a container-scope check, not just a visual eyeball (run 26):** `ScaledEmptyState`'s `cqmin` sizing resolves against the nearest ancestor with `container-type: size` — which today is set exactly once, at the whole-widget level (`WidgetRenderer.tsx`/`DraggableWindow.tsx`), not re-established at any nested sub-panel. Converting a hand-rolled empty state that lives inside a smaller bordered sub-panel (e.g. `ActivityWall/Widget.tsx`'s submissions card) makes the icon/text scale off the _full widget_, not the smaller panel — a real, visible size jump (in this case the icon roughly doubled, 24px→48px cap at default widget dimensions), not just a subtle rounding difference. `pnpm run validate`/`build` cannot catch this — it's a runtime CSS-scoping issue, not a type or test failure. Before converting any empty state that sits inside a sub-panel narrower than the full widget (as opposed to being the widget's only/full-bleed content), check whether that sub-panel establishes its own `container-type: size`; if not, treat the conversion as VISUAL-RISK requiring either a properly-scoped nested container boundary (careful — rescoping affects every other `cqmin` user in that panel, e.g. populated-state content) or a size-override affordance on `ScaledEmptyState`, not a straight swap. `ActivityWall/Widget.tsx:1877` hit this in run 26 (PR #2143, closed without merging after review caught it).
- **Background subagents (async `Agent` calls) can get stuck in a "wait for notification" loop when they themselves spawn a background process (run 26):** 3 of 5 dimension subagents this run ended their turn saying some version of "I'll pause here and wait for the validate command / monitor to notify me" — but nested background-process completion inside a subagent's own context doesn't generate a wake-up the way the top-level orchestrator's task-notifications do, so each just sat inert until resumed via `SendMessage`. Fix: when resuming a stuck agent, explicitly instruct it to block synchronously (`wait <PID>` or a polling loop, or just re-run the command in the foreground) and not end its turn until it has the actual result in hand. Consider adding a line to future dispatch prompts: "run validate/build in the foreground, not backgrounded — don't end your turn waiting for a notification that won't arrive."
- **Worktree staleness recurred a 3rd time, and it's the exact same commit again (run 27):** The D1 and D3 subagents' worktrees were both cut from `0adda31` — the identical stale base seen in runs 24 AND 25 — while D4's worktree that same dispatch was correctly based on current `dev-paul`. Run 26 (the concurrent session, see the note above) reported no staleness at all that night, so this isn't every-run — but the fact that `0adda31` specifically keeps recurring across separate nights, rather than "whatever `dev-paul` HEAD was N runs ago," suggests the underlying worktree-isolation mechanism may have a cached/pinned base snapshot from an earlier point (possibly container/environment setup time) rather than resolving current `origin/dev-paul` at dispatch time — worth escalating to a human/infra fix rather than continuing to treat it as a one-off per-agent fluke. Until fixed: the orchestrator MUST check `git merge-base HEAD origin/dev-paul` in every dimension worktree before trusting any diff or branch from it, extract-and-reapply on a fresh branch when stale, and never trust a subagent's own "worktree is fresh" self-report.
- **Subagents can return mid-task, having spawned their own background validate/build and then run out of turns waiting on it (run 27):** Confirms and adds to the run-26 note below on the same failure mode — the D1 and D4 subagents this run also ended with "I'll pause here and wait for the background task notification" instead of an actual result. The task-notification's `status: completed` is about the agent call returning, not about the underlying work being done — always inspect the worktree directly (`git status`, `git diff origin/dev-paul --stat`, `git log`) rather than trusting the prose result when a subagent's final message describes waiting rather than reporting outcomes. The orchestrator picked up validate/build directly in the worktree both times rather than resuming the subagent via `SendMessage`, which was faster and gave full visibility into the evidence anyway — a viable alternative to the run-26 note's "resume and tell it to block synchronously" fix when the orchestrator already has shell access to the same worktree.
- **Worktree staleness recurred a 2nd time, same night as a clean run (run 25):** The D3 subagent's worktree was again cut from a stale base (`0adda31`, ~30 commits behind `origin/dev-paul`'s `9e08914` — the same commit seen stale in run 24), while the D4 subagent's worktree that same run was correctly based on current `dev-paul`. This confirms the staleness is per-worktree-creation, not a systemic clock/cache issue — always check each worktree independently via `git merge-base HEAD origin/dev-paul` before trusting its branch, even when a sibling worktree from the same dispatch was fine. Repair procedure (same as run 24): extract the diff, discard the stale worktree/branch, cut a fresh branch from current `dev-paul`, reapply, re-validate.
- **D3 subagent repeated the run-5 `className="mb-1"` dead-code mistake (run 25):** When converting hand-rolled labels to `SettingsLabel`, the subagent passed `className="mb-1"` attempting to preserve the original spacing — this is dead code per the documented Tailwind-specificity gotcha (`mb-2` always wins). Orchestrator repair: strip the dead override, accept bare `<SettingsLabel>` with canonical `mb-2`. This is now the second time an agent has made this exact mistake (see run 5 note below) — if a 3rd occurrence happens, consider adding an explicit "do NOT pass className to override margin" line to the D3 dispatch prompt template, not just relying on agents reading this doc's Notes section.
- **SettingsLabel `htmlFor` pairing is worth doing at conversion time, not just noting (run 25):** gemini-code-assist flagged 3 of the 8 run-25 D3 conversions (inputs/textareas with a single, unambiguous adjacent control) for missing `useId()` + `htmlFor`/`id` pairing. This wasn't a regression (the original hand-rolled `<label>` elements didn't have `htmlFor` either), but since `SettingsLabel` already supports `htmlFor`, it's a low-cost improvement to add proactively when the label sits directly above exactly one input/textarea. Skip it when the label doesn't map to one clear control (e.g. "Available To" above a description + button grid, or "PDF File" above a button that triggers a hidden file input) — `htmlFor` on an ambiguous target is worse than omitting it.
- **Worktree base staleness can be severe, not just a few commits (run 24):** All 5 dimension subagents' isolated worktrees were created from commit `0adda31` while `origin/dev-paul` HEAD was already at `a39c9b7` — roughly 30 commits of drift, not the usual "slightly behind" case described in the run 7 note below. `git diff origin/dev-paul --stat` inside a worktree is the fast way to detect this (a huge, unrelated-looking diff means the base is stale, not that the agent misbehaved). Because D1/D2/D3/D5 shipped no changes this run it was harmless for them, but D4 did ship — the orchestrator's fix was to treat the agent's diff as a verified _patch_ (not a mergeable branch): discard the stale worktree/branch entirely, re-apply the same edits by hand on a fresh branch cut from current `dev-paul`, and re-run full validate there before committing. **Going forward: before trusting any subagent worktree's branch for integration, run `git merge-base HEAD origin/dev-paul` inside it and compare to `git rev-parse origin/dev-paul` — if they differ, rebase (or reapply) onto current `dev-paul` rather than pushing the branch as-is.**
- **Validate must be green before any run.** If already red, STOP and report — do not attempt consistency work on a broken baseline.
- **When updating this doc, diff against the LATEST `origin/dev-paul`, never blindly append.** Run 22 shipped as two separate same-night doc PRs (#2100 then #2108); the second PR's branch wasn't rebased onto the first's merge before opening, and the merge concatenated instead of replacing — the entire Run Log (run log rows 2026-06-27 through bootstrap) and the D3 backlog table got duplicated, bloating the file from ~35KB to 295KB over the following 3 days undetected (format-check only checks table alignment, not content duplication). Fixed in run 23 (net -142 lines). Before committing a doc update: re-fetch `origin/dev-paul`, rebase your log branch onto it, and sanity-check row counts (`grep -c '^| 20'` on the Run Log table) look like "previous count + this run's ~5-6 rows", not roughly double.
- **css-scaling.md guidance overrides CLAUDE.md on cqh/cqw:** Some widgets intentionally use `min(Xcqh, Ycqw)` for better aspect-ratio fill. The css-scaling.md journal explicitly marks these as "won't fix." Do not re-flag them.
- **The `--spart-primary` var is scoped to the dashboard container**, not the document root — it will not resolve in portaled elements rendered to `document.body`. Confirm render tree before using it.
- **ScaledEmptyState is `skipScaling: true`-aware** — it uses `cqmin` units internally; no additional scaling needed in the caller.
- **SettingsLabel is for settings back-face and admin config panels** — never use it in front-face widget content; settings panels do not need container query scaling.
- **Button text with uppercase tracking-widest is NOT SettingsLabel** — only section/field labels above form controls. Collapsible header buttons (e.g., in Schedule/Settings) are explicitly excepted (D3-E1, D3-E2).
- **D2 is fully aligned (run 3):** No remaining actionable inline-style hardcoded brand colors. All `#ad2122` instances are intentional exceptions. Future D2 audits only needed when a new widget is added.
- **D5 admin Toast pattern fully documented (run 3):** All remaining local Toast instances in admin components are intentional exceptions (D5-E2 through D5-E14). The pattern is inline-in-modal-body for z-index reasons — confirmed legitimate UX. `InstructionalRoutinesManager` was the last convertible instance. Future D5 runs should check NEW admin components only.
- **One unification per dimension per night.** Resist the urge to sweep all instances; the goal is preventing regrowth via enforcement, not a one-time manual sweep.
- **PollWidget/Settings.tsx D3 backlog entry is STALE** — file already uses SettingsLabel throughout. Closed in run 2 review.
- **Worktree isolation note (runs 2–5):** Agent worktrees sometimes write changes directly to the main working tree (`/home/user/SpartBoard/`) rather than only to their isolated worktree. After each run, verify the main worktree (`git status` on dev-paul) is clean before ending the session. If changes appear, inspect them: they may be valid dimension work that needs to be committed to a separate branch rather than dev-paul directly.

- **D3 lighter-weight label exceptions (run 8):** ExpectationsWidget and SoundWidget have labels with `text-slate-400 uppercase tracking-widest` but MISSING `font-black`. Converting to SettingsLabel would add `font-black` (changing visual weight). These are intentional lighter-weight variants classified as D3-E7, D3-E8, D3-E9.
- **D3 colored-callout heading exceptions (run 8):** MathTools/Settings.tsx h3 (brand-blue-dark, D3-E6) and RecessGear/Settings.tsx span (text-xs emerald, D3-E10) are intentional themed callout headings, not form section labels.
- **Worktree validate gotcha (run 6):** Running `pnpm run validate` from inside a worktree fails because the worktree doesn't have its own `node_modules` or `functions/node_modules`. Fix: symlink both from the main repo (`ln -sf <path-to-main-repo>/node_modules <worktree>/node_modules` and same for `functions/node_modules`). Alternatively, always run validate from the MAIN REPO after rebasing the branch there — cleaner and doesn't require symlinks.
- **D3 Tailwind specificity gotcha (run 5):** Passing `className="mb-1.5"` to `SettingsLabel` to override the built-in `mb-2` does NOT work. Tailwind's CSS declaration order means `mb-2` (declared later in the stylesheet, higher numeric value) always wins over `mb-1.5`. The `className` override becomes dead code. Always accept `SettingsLabel`'s canonical `mb-2` rather than trying to override it.
- **D3 Tailwind specificity gotcha applies below `mb-2` too, confirmed by compiling Tailwind's output (run 25, PR #2131 review):** The `mb-2`-always-wins rule isn't limited to overrides _larger_ than `mb-1.5` — it also beats attempts to go _smaller_. `className="mb-0"` does NOT zero out `SettingsLabel`'s margin either: `.mb-0` compiles to a rule _before_ `.mb-2` in Tailwind's generated stylesheet (verified via `npx tailwindcss` against a scratch file), so `mb-2` still wins. This came up converting `WorkSymbolsConfigurationModal.tsx`'s "Buildings" label, which sat in a `space-y-1.5` (6px) container with no label margin originally — post-conversion the collapsed gap grows to 8px (`mb-2`), and there is no working className fix. Backlog candidate: a `SettingsLabel` prop to opt out of the built-in `mb-2` (e.g. `noMargin` or `variant="compact"`) would be the real fix — needed by both this case and the recurring D3 NEEDS REVIEW lighter-weight-label cluster (MinTierSelect, NeedDoPutThen, NoteConfigurationPanel, TimeTool, NumberLine). Until that prop exists, treat small (≤4px) margin-collapse increases from conversion as accepted canonical alignment, same as the existing mb-1→mb-2 precedent.
